        <li hidden="hidden" data-menu-item="i6wiki-tab" data-targets="action-list.items" role="none" data-view-component="true" class="ActionListItem">
    
    
    <a tabindex="-1" id="item-72117c19-b72e-4783-9c38-92dff7a43021" href="/termux/termux-packages/wiki" role="menuitem" data-view-component="true" class="ActionListContent ActionListContent--visual16">
        <span class="ActionListItem-visual ActionListItem-visual--leading">
          <svg aria-hidden="true" height="16" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" data-view-component="true" class="octicon octicon-book">
    <path d="M0 1.75A.75.75 0 0 1 .75 1h4.253c1.227 0 2.317.59 3 1.501A3.743 3.743 0 0 1 11.006 1h4.245a.75.75 0 0 1 .75.75v10.5a.75.75 0 0 1-.75.75h-4.507a2.25 2.25 0 0 0-1.591.659l-.622.621a.75.75 0 0 1-1.06 0l-.622-.621A2.25 2.25 0 0 0 5.258 13H.75a.75.75 0 0 1-.75-.75Zm7.251 10.324.004-5.073-.002-2.253A2.25 2.25 0 0 0 5.003 2.5H1.5v9h3.757a3.75 3.75 0 0 1 1.994.574ZM8.755 4.75l-.004 7.322a3.752 3.752 0 0 1 1.992-.572H14.5v-9h-3.495a2.25 2.25 0 0 0-2.25 2.25Z"></path>

        <span data-view-component="true" class="ActionListItem-label">
          Wiki
</span>      
</a>
  
</li>
        <li hidden="hidden" data-menu-item="i7security-tab" data-targets="action-list.items" role="none" data-view-component="true" class="ActionListItem">

  </div>

  <div class="clearfix container-xl tmp-px-5 tmp-mt-4 page" data-hpc="true" id="wiki-wrapper">
    <div class="d-flex flex-column flex-md-row gh-header">
      <h1 class="flex-auto min-width-0 mb-2 mb-md-0 mr-0 mr-md-2 gh-header-title">Termux execution environment</h1>

        <div class="mt-0 mt-lg-1 flex-shrink-0 gh-header-actions">
          <a href="#wiki-pages-box" class="d-md-none ">Jump to bottom</a>

        </div>
    </div>

      <div class="mt-2 mt-md-1 tmp-pb-3 gh-header-meta">
        agnostic-apollo edited this page <relative-time datetime="2024-10-30T19:44:53Z" class="no-wrap">Oct 30, 2024</relative-time>
        &middot;
        <a href="/termux/termux-packages/wiki/Termux-execution-environment/_history" data-view-component="true" class="Link Link--underline">1 revision</a>
      </div>

    <div id="wiki-content" class="tmp-mt-4">
      <div data-view-component="true" class="Layout Layout--flowRow-until-md Layout--sidebarPosition-end Layout--sidebarPosition-flowRow-end">
  <div data-view-component="true" class="Layout-main">          <div id="wiki-body" class="gollum-markdown-content">
              <div class="markdown-body">
                <div class="markdown-heading"><h1 class="heading-element">Termux Execution Environment</h1><a id="user-content-termux-execution-environment" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Termux Execution Environment" href="#termux-execution-environment"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p>The following docs details how execution and dynamic linking happens in Termux, including issues/errors related to them and what path related environment variables are exported by Android and Termux by default.</p>
<div class="markdown-heading"><h3 class="heading-element">Contents</h3><a id="user-content-contents" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Contents" href="#contents"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<ul>
<li><a href="#execution">Execution</a></li>
<li><a href="#termux-app-child-process-forking">Termux App Child Process Forking</a></li>
<li><a href="#execution-errors">Execution Errors</a></li>
<li><a href="#dynamic-library-linking">Dynamic Library Linking</a></li>
<li><a href="#dynamic-library-linking-errors">Dynamic Library Linking Errors</a></li>
<li><a href="#listing-and-searching-libraries-and-symbols">Listing and Searching Libraries and Symbols</a></li>
<li><a href="#path-environment-variables">Path Environment Variables</a></li>
<li><a href="#path-environment-variables-exported-by-android">Path Environment Variables Exported By Android</a></li>
<li><a href="#path-environment-variables-exported-by-termux">Path Environment Variables Exported By Termux</a></li>
</ul>
<hr>
<p> </p>
<div class="markdown-heading"><h2 class="heading-element">Execution</h2><a id="user-content-execution" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Execution" href="#execution"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p><strong>Termux executes programs natively on <a href="https://source.android.com/docs/core/architecture" rel="nofollow">Android host OS</a></strong> by default, without any emulation or containerization (docker/VM/chroot/proot), and uses the <a href="https://source.android.com/docs/core/architecture/kernel" rel="nofollow">Android host kernel</a> underneath, which is based on <a href="https://www.kernel.org/linux.html" rel="nofollow">Linux kernel</a>, and does not use a custom kernel. Programs are compiled with Android <a href="https://developer.android.com/ndk/guides" rel="nofollow"><code>NDK</code></a> and dynamically linked against Android system <code>bionic</code> (<a href="https://cs.android.com/android/platform/superproject/+/android-14.0.0_r1:bionic/README.md" rel="nofollow">1</a>, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bionic_(software)" rel="nofollow">2</a>) libraries under <code>/system/lib[64]</code>, which also provides <a href="https://cs.android.com/android/platform/superproject/+/android-14.0.0_r1:bionic/libc" rel="nofollow"><code>libc</code></a> as <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/C_standard_library" rel="nofollow">C standard library</a>. Programs are not linked against <code>glibc</code> (<a href="https://www.gnu.org/software/libc" rel="nofollow">1</a>, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glibc" rel="nofollow">2</a>) like done on other linux distros, like <a href="https://www.debian.org" rel="nofollow"><code>debian</code></a>, and hence there are differences between the two, i.e <code>bionic</code> is not as featured and ported programs may require patches. Check <a href="https://wiki.termux.com/wiki/Differences_from_Linux#Termux_uses_Bionic_libc" rel="nofollow">here</a> for some differences.</p>
<p>However, support for emulation is also optionally available for the user with <code>proot</code> (<a href="https://github.com/proot-me/PRoot/">1</a>, <a href="https://github.com/termux/proot">2</a>, <a href="https://wiki.termux.com/wiki/PRoot" rel="nofollow">3</a>, <a href="https://github.com/termux/termux-packages/tree/master/packages/proot">4</a>) and <code>qemu</code> (<a href="https://www.qemu.org/" rel="nofollow">1</a>, <a href="https://github.com/termux/termux-packages/tree/master/packages/qemu-system-x86-64-headless">2</a>) without <code>root</code>, and also for <code>chroot</code> (<a href="https://man7.org/linux/man-pages/man2/chroot.2.html" rel="nofollow">1</a>, <a href="https://man7.org/linux/man-pages/man1/chroot.1.html" rel="nofollow">2</a>, <a href="https://github.com/termux/termux-packages/tree/master/packages/coreutils">3</a>) with <code>root</code>.</p>
<p>For info on how Termux app forks child processes from its main <code>app</code> process to run foreground terminals (<code>TermuxSessions</code>) or a background tasks (<code>TermuxTasks</code>), check <a href="#termux-app-child-process-forking">Termux App Child Process Forking</a> section below.</p>
<p>For info on execution errors, check <a href="#execution-errors">Execution Errors</a> section below.</p>
<p>For info on <code>$PATH</code>, <code>$LD_LIBRARY_PATH</code>, <code>$LD_PRELOAD</code> environment variables exported by Android and Termux for execution and dynamic linking, check <a href="#path-environment-variables">Path Environment Variables</a>, <a href="#path-environment-variables-exported-by-android">Path Environment Variables Exported By Android</a>, <a href="#path-environment-variables-exported-by-termux">Path Environment Variables Exported By Termux</a>.</p>
<p>For info on Android and Termux filesystems, and Termux private app data directory, check <a href="#./Termux-file-system-layout">Termux Filesystem Layout</a> docs.</p>
<p><strong>Termux packages</strong> in the app bootstrap (<a href="https://github.com/termux/termux-app/blob/899ef71e/app/build.gradle#L213-L232">1</a>, <a href="https://github.com/termux/termux-packages/wiki/For-maintainers#bootstraps">2</a>), <a href="https://packages.termux.dev/" rel="nofollow">primary packages repository</a> and its <a href="https://github.com/termux/termux-packages/wiki/Mirrors">mirrors</a> <strong>are specifically compiled for the <code>rootfs</code> directory <code>/data/data/com.termux/files</code>, based on the Termux app package name <code>com.termux</code> and the expected <a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/content/pm/ApplicationInfo#dataDir" rel="nofollow">private app data directory</a> <code>/data/data/com.termux</code></strong> android would assign to the app on installation if its installed on the primary user <code>0</code> of the device. These packages would not work for any other app package name or a different app data or <code>rootfs</code> directory, and packages must be compiled specifically for any such changes, like in case forking the app with a different package name or installing Termux app on a <a href="https://source.android.com/docs/devices/admin/multi-user" rel="nofollow">secondary user</a>, <a href="https://developer.android.com/work/managed-profiles" rel="nofollow">work profile</a> or <a href="https://source.android.com/docs/core/storage/adoptable" rel="nofollow">adoptable storage</a>. In addition to the <code>rootfs</code> directory, the <code>core</code> and <code>apps</code> directories are also used by the Termux apps and certain packages for certain things. During build time, the <code>termux-packages</code> <a href="https://github.com/termux/termux-packages/blob/7b253ac2/build-package.sh#L366"><code>build-package.sh</code></a> scripts loads the app package name and directory paths that are set in <a href="https://github.com/termux/termux-packages/blob/master/scripts/properties.sh"><code>properties.sh</code></a>, which are primarily defined by the <code>$TERMUX_APP__PACKAGE_NAME</code>, <code>$TERMUX_APP__DATA_DIR</code>, <code>$TERMUX__PROJECT_DIR</code>, <code>$TERMUX__CORE_DIR</code>, <code>$TERMUX__APPS_DIR</code>, <code>$TERMUX__ROOTFS</code>, <code>$TERMUX__HOME</code>, and <code>$TERMUX__PREFIX</code> variables. Check <a href="https://github.com/termux/termux-packages/wiki/Build-environment">Build environment</a> and <a href="https://github.com/termux/termux-packages/wiki/Building-packages">Building packages</a> docs for more info on how packages are built.</p>
<p>For info on which packages are available on Termux app installation by default and how they are built, check <a href="https://github.com/termux/termux-packages/wiki/For-maintainers#bootstraps">bootstrap</a> docs.</p>
<hr>
<p> </p>
<div class="markdown-heading"><h2 class="heading-element">Termux App Child Process Forking</h2><a id="user-content-termux-app-child-process-forking" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Termux App Child Process Forking" href="#termux-app-child-process-forking"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p>When Android starts an Termux app, it only creates a single main <code>app</code> process for it with the process name that equals its package name <code>com.termux</code>. (<a href="https://developer.android.com/guide/components/processes-and-threads" rel="nofollow">1</a>, <a href="https://developer.android.com/guide/components/activities/process-lifecycle" rel="nofollow">2</a>) Moreover, no additional <a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/app/Service" rel="nofollow">service</a> <a href="https://developer.android.com/guide/topics/manifest/service-element#proc" rel="nofollow"><code>process</code></a> or <a href="https://developer.android.com/guide/topics/manifest/service-element#isolated" rel="nofollow"><code>isolatedProcess</code></a> are used by Termux.</p>
<p>When Termux app needs to start foreground terminals (<code>TermuxSessions</code>) or background tasks (<code>TermuxTasks</code>), to run a <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shell_(computing)" rel="nofollow">shell</a>, binary or script command, it <a href="https://man7.org/linux/man-pages/man2/fork.2.html" rel="nofollow">forks</a> a child process from its main <code>app</code> process and then calls one of the <a href="https://man7.org/linux/man-pages/man3/exec.3p.html" rel="nofollow"><code>exec()</code></a> family of functions in the child process to replace it with the desired command. These child processes are called phantom processes internally by Android, i.e any process that has been forked from the main <code>app</code> process and is now either a child of the <code>app</code> process or of <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Init" rel="nofollow"><code>init</code></a> process, <strong>check <a href="https://github.com/agnostic-apollo/Android-Docs/blob/master/en/docs/apps/processes/phantom-cached-and-empty-processes.md">Phantom, Cached And Empty Processes</a> docs for more info on phantom processes.</strong></p>
<p>The <code>exec()</code> family of functions are <a href="https://cs.android.com/android/platform/superproject/+/android-14.0.0_r1:bionic/libc/include/unistd.h;l=92-100" rel="nofollow">declared in <code>unistd.h</code></a> and <a href="https://cs.android.com/android/platform/superproject/+/android-14.0.0_r1:bionic/libc/bionic/exec.cpp" rel="nofollow">implemented by <code>exec.cpp</code></a> in android <code>bionic</code> <code>libc</code> library. The <code>exec()</code> functions are wrappers around the <a href="https://cs.android.com/android/platform/superproject/+/android-14.0.0_r1:bionic/libc/SYSCALLS.TXT;l=68" rel="nofollow"><code>execve()</code></a> system call listed in <a href="https://man7.org/linux/man-pages/man2/syscalls.2.html" rel="nofollow"><code>syscalls(2)</code></a> provided by the <a href="https://cs.android.com/android/kernel/superproject/+/ebe69964:common/include/linux/syscalls.h;l=790" rel="nofollow">android/linux kernel</a>, which can also be directly called with the <a href="https://man7.org/linux/man-pages/man2/syscall.2.html" rel="nofollow"><code>syscall(2)</code></a> library function <a href="https://cs.android.com/android/platform/superproject/+/android-14.0.0_r1:bionic/libc/include/unistd.h;l=308" rel="nofollow">declared in <code>unistd.h</code></a>. Note that there is also a <code>execve()</code> wrapper in <code>unistd.h</code> around the <code>execve()</code> system call.</p>
<p>The <a href="https://github.com/termux/termux-exec"><code>termux-exec</code></a> library is also loaded with <code>$LD_PRELOAD</code> when commands are executed, which overrides the entire <code>exec()</code> family of functions, but will not override direct calls to the <code>execve()</code> system call via <code>syscall(2)</code>, which is usually not directly called by programs. It overrides the functions to solve the issues related to <a href="#app-data-file-execute-restrictions">App Data File Execute Restrictions</a> and <a href="#linux-vs-termux-bin-paths">Linux vs Termux <code>bin</code> paths</a> when exec-ing files in Termux. Check <a href="https://github.com/termux/termux-exec/blob/master/site/pages/en/projects/docs/technical/index.md#app-data-file-execute-restrictions"><code>termux-exec</code> <code>exec()</code></a> docs for more info.</p>
<p><strong>See also:</strong></p>
<ul>
<li><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Exec_(system_call)" rel="nofollow">exec (system call) wiki</a></li>
<li><a href="https://pubs.opengroup.org/onlinepubs/7908799/xsh/unistd.h.html" rel="nofollow"><code>unistd.h</code> POSIX spec</a></li>
<li><a href="https://pubs.opengroup.org/onlinepubs/7908799/xsh/execve.html" rel="nofollow"><code>execve</code> POSIX spec</a></li>
<li><a href="https://man7.org/linux/man-pages/man2/execve.2.html" rel="nofollow"><code>execve(2)</code> linux man</a></li>
<li><a href="https://man7.org/linux/man-pages/man3/exec.3.html" rel="nofollow"><code>exec(3)</code> linux man</a></li>
<li><a href="https://man7.org/linux/man-pages/man3/exec.3p.html" rel="nofollow"><code>exec(3p)</code> linux man</a></li>
<li><a href="https://pubs.opengroup.org/onlinepubs/7908799/xsh/fork.html" rel="nofollow"><code>fork</code> POSIX spec</a></li>
<li><a href="https://man7.org/linux/man-pages/man2/fork.2.html" rel="nofollow"><code>fork(2)</code> linux man</a></li>
</ul>
<p> </p>
<p>Termux uses <code>Runtime.exec()</code> for <code>TermuxTasks</code> and <code>execvp()</code> for <code>TermuxSessions</code> to fork processes from its main <code>app</code> process. The new child processes that are started may then call the <code>exec()</code> family of functions to fork even more nested child processes.</p>
<div class="markdown-heading"><h3 class="heading-element">
<code>Runtime.exec()</code> Java Function</h3><a id="user-content-runtimeexec-java-function" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Runtime.exec() Java Function" href="#runtimeexec-java-function"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p>The <a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/java/lang/Runtime#exec(java.lang.String%5B%5D,%20java.lang.String%5B%5D)" rel="nofollow"><code>Runtime.exec()</code></a> is the <code>Java</code> API that forks a child processes and calls <code>execvpe()</code>. The parent of the child process remains the main <code>app</code> process itself.</p>
<p>Termux uses this for running background <a href="https://github.com/termux/termux-app/blob/v0.118.0/termux-shared/src/main/java/com/termux/shared/shell/TermuxTask.java"><code>TermuxTasks</code></a>, which are managed by the foreground <a href="https://github.com/termux/termux-app/blob/v0.118.0/app/src/main/java/com/termux/app/TermuxService.java#L86"><code>TermuxService</code></a>. These background tasks can be sent via the <a href="https://github.com/termux/termux-app/wiki/RUN_COMMAND-Intent"><code>RUN_COMMAND Intent</code></a> and by Termux plugins like <a href="https://github.com/termux/termux-boot"><code>termux-boot</code></a>, <a href="https://github.com/termux/termux-tasker"><code>termux-tasker</code></a> and <a href="https://github.com/termux/termux-widget"><code>termux-widget</code></a>. They show as <code>&lt;n&gt; tasks</code> in the <code>Termux</code> notification.</p>
<p><strong>Call stack:</strong> <a href="https://cs.android.com/android/platform/superproject/+/android-12.0.0_r32:libcore/ojluni/src/main/java/java/lang/Runtime.java;l=694" rel="nofollow"><code>Runtime.exec()</code></a> -&gt; <a href="https://cs.android.com/android/platform/superproject/+/android-12.0.0_r32:libcore/ojluni/src/main/java/java/lang/ProcessBuilder.java;l=1029" rel="nofollow"><code>ProcessBuilder.start()</code></a> -&gt; <a href="https://cs.android.com/android/platform/superproject/+/android-12.0.0_r32:libcore/ojluni/src/main/java/java/lang/ProcessImpl.java;l=137" rel="nofollow"><code>ProcessImpl.start()</code></a> -&gt; <a href="https://cs.android.com/android/platform/superproject/+/android-12.0.0_r32:libcore/ojluni/src/main/java/java/lang/UNIXProcess.java;l=133" rel="nofollow"><code>UNIXProcess()</code></a> -&gt; <a href="https://cs.android.com/android/platform/superproject/+/android-12.0.0_r32:libcore/ojluni/src/main/native/UNIXProcess_md.c;l=926" rel="nofollow"><code>UNIXProcess_md.forkAndExec()</code></a> -&gt; <a href="https://cs.android.com/android/platform/superproject/+/android-12.0.0_r32:libcore/ojluni/src/main/native/UNIXProcess_md.c;l=847" rel="nofollow"><code>UNIXProcess_md.startChild()</code></a> (<a href="https://cs.android.com/android/platform/superproject/+/android-12.0.0_r32:libcore/ojluni/src/main/native/UNIXProcess_md.c;l=68" rel="nofollow">note on forking</a> for <a href="https://manpages.debian.org/testing/manpages-dev/clone.2.en.html" rel="nofollow"><code>clone()</code></a>, <a href="https://manpages.debian.org/testing/manpages-dev/vfork.2.en.html" rel="nofollow"><code>vfork()</code></a> and <a href="https://manpages.debian.org/testing/manpages-dev/fork.2.en.html" rel="nofollow"><code>fork()</code></a> usage) -&gt; <a href="https://cs.android.com/android/platform/superproject/+/android-12.0.0_r32:libcore/ojluni/src/main/native/UNIXProcess_md.c;l=782" rel="nofollow"><code>UNIXProcess_md.childProcess()</code></a> -&gt; <a href="https://cs.android.com/android/platform/superproject/+/android-12.0.0_r32:libcore/ojluni/src/main/native/UNIXProcess_md.c;l=603" rel="nofollow"><code>UNIXProcess_md.JDK_execvpe()</code></a> -&gt; <a href="https://cs.android.com/android/platform/superproject/+/android-12.0.0_r32:bionic/libc/bionic/exec.cpp;l=119" rel="nofollow"><code>exec.execvpe()</code></a></p>
<div class="markdown-heading"><h3 class="heading-element">
<code>exec()</code> C Function</h3><a id="user-content-exec-c-function" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: exec() C Function" href="#exec-c-function"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p>The <code>execvp()</code> is part of the native <code>exec()</code> family of functions that replaces the current process image with a new process image. This can be called by the child process that has been spawned from the <code>app</code> process after it calls <code>fork()</code>. These functions can be called in native <code>c/c++</code> code via <a href="https://docs.oracle.com/javase/8/docs/technotes/guides/jni/spec/intro.html" rel="nofollow"><code>JNI</code></a> by an app.</p>
<p>Termux uses this for running foreground <a href="https://github.com/termux/termux-app/blob/v0.118.0/termux-shared/src/main/java/com/termux/shared/shell/TermuxSession.java#L131"><code>TermuxSessions</code></a>, which are managed by the foreground <a href="https://github.com/termux/termux-app/blob/v0.118.0/app/src/main/java/com/termux/app/TermuxService.java#L78"><code>TermuxService</code></a>. The <code>TermuxSession</code> creates a <code>TerminalSession</code> that calls <a href="https://github.com/termux/termux-app/blob/v0.118.0/terminal-emulator/src/main/java/com/termux/terminal/TerminalSession.java#L127"><code>create_subprocess</code></a> via <code>JNI</code> defined in <a href="https://github.com/termux/termux-app/blob/v0.118.0/terminal-emulator/src/main/jni/termux.c#L25"><code>termux.c</code></a>, which then calls <a href="https://github.com/termux/termux-app/blob/v0.118.0/terminal-emulator/src/main/jni/termux.c#L63"><code>fork()</code></a> and the child process calls <a href="https://github.com/termux/termux-app/blob/v0.118.0/terminal-emulator/src/main/jni/termux.c#L106"><code>execvp()</code></a>. By default, if no custom command is passed to run in the <code>TerminalSession</code>, the <code>/data/data/com.termux/files/usr/bin/login</code> script is called, which runs <a href="https://github.com/termux/termux-packages/blob/master/packages/termux-tools/login#L35"><code>exec "$SHELL"</code></a> to replace itself with the <code>login</code> shell defined, which defaults to <code>/data/data/com.termux/files/usr/bin/bash</code>.</p>
<div class="markdown-heading"><h3 class="heading-element">
<code>daemon</code> C Function</h3><a id="user-content-daemon-c-function" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: daemon C Function" href="#daemon-c-function"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p>The <a href="https://man7.org/linux/man-pages/man3/daemon.3.html" rel="nofollow"><code>daemon()</code></a> function is for programs wishing to detach themselves from the controlling terminal and run in the background as <a href="https://man7.org/linux/man-pages/man7/daemon.7.html" rel="nofollow">system daemons</a>. The child process forked from the parent process basically detaches itself from the parent so that it is no longer its parent process (<code>ppid</code>) and is inherited by the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Init" rel="nofollow"><code>init</code></a> (<code>pid</code> <code>1</code>) process.</p>
<p>Termux app does not start daemons itself but it can be done by programs that may be started by users themselves, like with <code>sshd</code> and <code>crond</code> commands. If <code>sshd</code> command is run, the <code>ps</code> output will show <code>sshd</code> to have <code>init</code> (<code>pid</code> <code>1</code>) as the <code>ppid</code>, instead of <code>pid</code> of its original parent <code>bash</code>. These daemons have a higher chance of getting killed since there are no longer attached to the <code>app</code> process. Optionally, processes may not be <a href="https://github.com/termux/termux-app/issues/2015#issuecomment-860492160">daemonized</a> (like by running <code>sshd -D</code>) and kept in the foreground so that they are still tied to the <code>app</code> process as that would make it less likely for them to get killed, assuming <a href="https://github.com/agnostic-apollo/Android-Docs/blob/master/en/docs/apps/processes/phantom-cached-and-empty-processes.md#commands-to-disable-phantom-process-killing-and-tldr">phantom process killer has been disabled</a>. Some vendors also have additional daemon process killers.</p>
<hr>
<p> </p>
<div class="markdown-heading"><h2 class="heading-element">Execution Errors</h2><a id="user-content-execution-errors" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Execution Errors" href="#execution-errors"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p>The following issues may occur when executing files in termux.</p>
<ul>
<li><a href="#file-execution-and-special-file-features-not-allowed-in-external-storage">File Execution And Special File Features Not Allowed In External Storage</a></li>
<li><a href="#some-files-cannot-be-executed-under-system-bin">Some Files Cannot Be Executed Under <code>/system/bin</code></a></li>
<li><a href="#path-contains-incompatible-directory-paths"><code>$PATH</code> contains incompatible directory paths</a></li>
<li><a href="#app-data-file-execute-restrictions">App Data File Execute Restrictions</a></li>
<li><a href="#linux-vs-termux-bin-paths">Linux vs Termux <code>bin</code> paths</a></li>
</ul>
<p> </p>
<div class="markdown-heading"><h3 class="heading-element">File Execution And Special File Features Not Allowed In External Storage</h3><a id="user-content-file-execution-and-special-file-features-not-allowed-in-external-storage" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: File Execution And Special File Features Not Allowed In External Storage" href="#file-execution-and-special-file-features-not-allowed-in-external-storage"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p>The shared/public/primary external storage for internal sd card or for external sd card in device slot formatted as <a href="https://source.android.com/docs/core/storage/adoptable" rel="nofollow">adoptable storage</a> is mounted at <code>/storage/emulated/&lt;user_id&gt;</code> (or its shortcut <code>/sdcard</code>), and reliable secondary external storage for external sd card in device slot formatted as <a href="https://source.android.com/docs/core/storage" rel="nofollow">portable storage</a> are mounted at <code>/storage/XXXX-XXXX</code>. These mounts <strong>emulate the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File_Allocation_Table#FAT32" rel="nofollow"><code>fat32</code> filesystem</a></strong> and use the <code>sdcardfs</code> (<a href="https://cs.android.com/android/platform/superproject/+/android-14.0.0_r1:system/core/sdcard/sdcard.cpp;l=122" rel="nofollow">1</a>) or <code>fuse</code> (<a href="https://cs.android.com/android/platform/superproject/+/android-14.0.0_r1:system/vold/Utils.cpp;l=1636" rel="nofollow">1</a>, <a href="https://cs.android.com/android/_/android/platform/system/vold/+/a438b2436886a9d1dbb865c891cc5ec9ececba09" rel="nofollow">2</a>) filesystems depending on Android version/build, (<a href="https://source.android.com/docs/core/storage/fuse-passthrough" rel="nofollow">1</a>, <a href="https://source.android.com/docs/core/storage/sdcardfs-deprecate" rel="nofollow">2</a>) and <strong>use the <code>noexec</code> <code>mount</code> flag</strong>. These mounts and are accessible to apps with direct file-access if storage permission (<a href="https://developer.android.com/training/data-storage/manage-all-files" rel="nofollow">1</a>, <a href="https://github.com/termux/termux-app/issues/71#issuecomment-1869222653">2</a>) is granted or via <a href="https://developer.android.com/guide/topics/providers/document-provider" rel="nofollow">SAF APIs</a>. The <code>Android/data</code> and <code>Android/obb</code> directories are mounted with a <code>tmpfs</code> filesystem and also have the <code>noexec</code> <code>mount</code> flag. (<a href="https://cs.android.com/android/platform/superproject/+/android-14.0.0_r1:system/vold/VolumeManager.cpp;l=737-749" rel="nofollow">1</a>)</p>
<p>The reliable secondary external storage for external sd card in device slot is initially mounted at <code>/mnt/media_rw/XXXX-XXXX</code> with their original filesystem before being mounted at <code>/storage/XXXX-XXXX</code> with an emulated filesystem. The unreliable secondary external storages, like for USB OTG drives are only mounted at <code>/mnt/media_rw/XXXX-XXXX</code> with their original filesystem, but not mounted at <code>/storage/XXXX-XXXX</code> with an emulated filesystem. These initial mounts primarily only support the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/ExFAT" rel="nofollow"><code>exfat</code></a> (<a href="https://cs.android.com/android/platform/superproject/+/android-14.0.0_r1:system/vold/model/PublicVolume.cpp;l=150" rel="nofollow">1</a>, <a href="https://cs.android.com/android/platform/superproject/+/android-14.0.0_r1:system/vold/fs/Exfat.cpp;l=60" rel="nofollow">2</a>) and related filesystems, or in some cases the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ext4" rel="nofollow"><code>ext4</code></a> (<a href="https://cs.android.com/android/platform/superproject/+/android-14.0.0_r1:system/vold/model/PrivateVolume.cpp;l=143" rel="nofollow">1</a>, <a href="https://cs.android.com/android/platform/superproject/+/android-14.0.0_r1:system/vold/fs/Ext4.cpp;l=134" rel="nofollow">2</a>) filesystem, and also use the <code>noexec</code> <code>mount</code> flag. The <code>/mnt/media_rw/XXXX-XXXX</code> mounts for reliable storages are not accessible to apps without root access. The <code>/mnt/media_rw/XXXX-XXXX</code> mounts for unreliable storages are accessible to apps with root access, or with the <a href="https://cs.android.com/android/platform/superproject/+/android-14.0.0_r1:frameworks/base/core/res/AndroidManifest.xml;l=1241" rel="nofollow"><code>MANAGE_EXTERNAL_STORAGE</code></a> permission on Android <code>&gt;= 12</code>. (<a href="https://github.com/termux/termux-app/issues/71#issuecomment-1869222653">1</a>)</p>
<p>Following are some of the features not supported by external storage filesystems like at <code>/sdcard</code>/<code>/storage/emulated/0</code> that emulate a <code>fat</code> filesystem, which are <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Comparison_of_file_systems" rel="nofollow">supported by other filesystems</a> that are commonly used on Linux distros and for Android private app data directory, like <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ext4" rel="nofollow"><code>ext4</code></a> or <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/F2FS" rel="nofollow"><code>f2fs</code></a> filesystems.</p>
<ul>
<li>
<strong>Files cannot be executed directly with their path</strong> due to the <a href="https://manpages.debian.org/testing/mount/mount.8.en.html" rel="nofollow"><code>noexec</code> <code>mount</code> flag</a>, like with <code>/sdcard/file</code> or <code>./file</code>. However, if the file is script file instead of a binary file, then it can be passed to its respective shell for it to be executed, like with <code>bash /sdcard/script</code>. However, it is <strong>highly recommended to not execute files on public storages</strong> that can be accessed by other apps as it is a <strong>huge security risk</strong>, since other malicious apps could modify such files and when user executes them in Termux, malicious code could run in Termux user context, or even <code>root</code> user context if Termux app has been granted root permissions.</li>
<li><strong>No hard or soft symlink files can be created.</strong></li>
<li>
<strong>Files do support modifications of file permissions or ownership attributes</strong>.</li>
<li>
<strong>Filenames are <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File_system#File_names" rel="nofollow">case insensitive</a></strong>, i.e <code>foo</code> and <code>FOO</code> and <code>FoO</code>, etc would be considered the same file.</li>
</ul>
<p>Due, to these issues, <strong>using external storage directories will cause problems for certain programs</strong>, like creating <code>git</code> repositories or building software that require special features, check <a href="https://github.com/termux/termux-app/issues/3385"><code>termux/termux-app#3385</code></a> and <a href="https://github.com/termux/termux-app/issues/3777"><code>termux/termux-app#3777</code></a>.</p>
<p>However, the <strong><a href="./Termux-file-system-layout#termux-private-app-data-directory">Termux private app data directory</a> is not mounted with the <code>noexec</code> <code>mount</code> flag, and is usually the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ext4" rel="nofollow"><code>ext4</code></a> or <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/F2FS" rel="nofollow"><code>f2fs</code></a> filesystem</strong>, which supports symlinks and other file attributes. This directory is also <strong>not accessible to any other app by default and is safe to use</strong>, unless access is explicitly granted by user to it by installing a <a href="https://developer.android.com/guide/topics/manifest/manifest-element#uid" rel="nofollow"><code>sharedUserId</code></a> plugin app or via Storage Access Framework (SAF) or Termux APIs.</p>
<p>It is <strong>highly recommended to only keep Termux files under its <code>$HOME</code> (<code>~/</code>) or <code>$TERMUX__PREFIX</code> directories</strong>, but not <code>~/storage</code> directories as directories under it would be symlinks to external storage directories created by <a href="https://wiki.termux.com/wiki/Termux-setup-storage" rel="nofollow"><code>termux-setup-storage</code></a>.</p>
<div class="markdown-heading"><h2 class="heading-element"> </h2><a id="" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink:  " href="#"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p> </p>
<div class="markdown-heading"><h3 class="heading-element">Some Files Cannot Be Executed Under <code>/system/bin</code>
</h3><a id="user-content-some-files-cannot-be-executed-under-systembin" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Some Files Cannot Be Executed Under /system/bin" href="#some-files-cannot-be-executed-under-systembin"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p>The Android system provided executables that primarily exist under <code>/system/bin</code> cannot all be executed by all apps and users as Android has different protections in place.</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>The files are assigned different <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File-system_permissions#Traditional_Unix_permissions" rel="nofollow">ownership and permissions</a> (<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Discretionary_access_control" rel="nofollow">DAC</a>) by Android. This prevents some executables from being executed by app processes or even the <code>shell</code> user. Most files have the <code>root:shell</code> ownership and <code>rwxr-xr-x</code> permissions, allowing <code>read</code> and <code>execute</code> by <code>other</code> users. However, some files like <a href="https://cs.android.com/android/platform/superproject/+/android-14.0.0_r1:external/selinux/secilc/README" rel="nofollow"><code>secilc</code></a> and <a href="https://cs.android.com/android/platform/superproject/+/android-14.0.0_r1:bootable/recovery/uncrypt" rel="nofollow"><code>uncrypt</code></a> have <code>root:root</code> ownership and do not allow <code>other</code> users to <code>execute</code> them, including the <code>shell</code> user. Some files like, <a href="https://cs.android.com/android/platform/superproject/+/android-14.0.0_r1:system/core/run-as/" rel="nofollow"><code>run-as</code></a> have <code>root:shell</code> ownership, but <code>rwxr-x---</code> permissions, preventing any <code>other</code> user than <code>root</code> or <code>shell</code> to <code>execute</code> them. Attempting to execute such files with the wrong user would result in the <code>Permission denied</code> error.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The files are assigned different <a href="https://source.android.com/docs/security/features/selinux" rel="nofollow">SeLinux</a> <a href="https://github.com/agnostic-apollo/Android-Docs/blob/master/site/pages/en/projects/docs/os/selinux/context-types.md#file-context-types">file context types</a> (<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mandatory_access_control" rel="nofollow">MAC</a>) by Android. (<a href="https://cs.android.com/android/platform/superproject/+/android-14.0.0_r1:system/sepolicy/private/file_contexts;l=222-388" rel="nofollow">1</a>) There are around <code>92</code> different context types on Android <code>14</code>. Different SeLinux policies exist for different <a href="https://github.com/agnostic-apollo/Android-Docs/blob/master/site/pages/en/projects/docs/os/selinux/context-types.md#process-context-types">process context types</a> which define whether a process can execute a file with a specific file context. (<a href="https://source.android.com/docs/security/features/selinux/customize#policy-placement" rel="nofollow">1</a>, <a href="https://cs.android.com/android/platform/superproject/+/android-14.0.0_r1:system/sepolicy/public" rel="nofollow">2</a>, <a href="https://cs.android.com/android/platform/superproject/+/android-14.0.0_r1:system/sepolicy/private" rel="nofollow">3</a>) This prevents some executables from being executed by app processes or even the <code>shell</code> user. For example, <code>auditctl</code> requires executing it as the <code>root</code> user. Attempting to execute such files with the wrong user will result in the <code>inaccessible or not found</code> error and a <a href="https://source.android.com/docs/security/features/selinux/validate" rel="nofollow">SeLinux <code>avc</code> denied</a> message will be logged in <a href="https://developer.android.com/tools/logcat" rel="nofollow"><code>logcat</code></a>, like <code> avc:  denied  { getattr } for  path="/system/bin/auditctl" dev="dm-6" ino=161 scontext=u:r:shell:s0 tcontext=u:object_r:auditctl_exec:s0 tclass=file</code>. Getting file attributes, like with <code>ls</code> will also fail for such files if not running as allowed user like <code>root</code>. There are also SeLinux policies other than for process/file context types that trigger other errors, <a href="https://github.com/termux/termux-packages/discussions/8292#discussioncomment-5102555">like for the <code>cmd</code> command</a>.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>There are additional internal checks during execution for calling <code>uid</code> and calling packages as well. Some commands can only be executed by privileged users like <code>root</code> or <code>shell</code>, like <a href="https://cs.android.com/android/_/android/platform/frameworks/base/+/3ef3f18ba3094c4cc4f954ba23d1da421f9ca8b0" rel="nofollow"><code>am</code> command can only be executed by them on Android <code>&gt;= 14</code></a>. Some commands, like ones that are run through <code>svc</code> may require a package name, and cannot be executed as <code>root</code>, since it does not have a package name, and requires running them as the <code>shell</code> user, which does have the <code>com.android.shell</code> package name.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The are additional internal checks during execution for whether the process has been granted a <a href="https://developer.android.com/guide/topics/permissions/overview" rel="nofollow">permission</a> to be able to run the specified command. The permissions are declared in the Android framework <code>AndroidManifest.xml</code> under <a href="https://cs.android.com/android/platform/superproject/+/android-14.0.0_r1:frameworks/base/core/res/AndroidManifest.xml;l=832" rel="nofollow"><code>Runtime permissions</code></a> or <a href="https://cs.android.com/android/platform/superproject/+/android-14.0.0_r1:frameworks/base/core/res/AndroidManifest.xml;l=1875" rel="nofollow"><code>Install permissions</code></a> sections.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>The <code>shell</code> (<code>2000</code>) user for the <code>com.android.shell</code> app package, and for commands that are run with <code>adb shell</code> (here <code>shell</code> refers to <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Unix_shell" rel="nofollow">CLI</a>, not the user) is a privileged user on Android that is allowed to run a lot of things and make lot of changes, however, it is generally not as privileged as the root user, other than when a package name is required. It has additional SeLinux policies that allow it to execute certain commands that cannot be executed by <a href="https://github.com/agnostic-apollo/Android-Docs/blob/master/site/pages/en/projects/docs/os/selinux/context-types.md#untrusted_app">untrusted app processes</a>, like ones that give it access to call specific android internal services. (<a href="https://cs.android.com/android/platform/superproject/+/android-14.0.0_r1:frameworks/base/packages/Shell/AndroidManifest.xml;l=20" rel="nofollow">1</a>, <a href="https://cs.android.com/android/platform/superproject/+/android-14.0.0_r1:system/sepolicy/private/shell.te" rel="nofollow">2</a>, <a href="https://cs.android.com/android/platform/superproject/+/android-14.0.0_r1:system/sepolicy/public/shell.te" rel="nofollow">3</a>) It also has additional <a href="https://cs.android.com/android/platform/superproject/+/android-14.0.0_r1:frameworks/base/packages/Shell/AndroidManifest.xml;l=25-844" rel="nofollow">permissions granted to it by default by Android</a> that are checked when certain commands are run, like for <code>cmd</code>, <code>am</code>, <code>pm</code> and <code>svc</code> commands.</p>
<p>Following is a truncated list of executables under <code>/system/bin</code> that are available on Android <code>14</code>, only some of the commonly used commands are listed for brevity.</p>
